# Build a new version of the dev-tools container.
# Updaing the Fedora version and adding Podman.
#[user@desktop]

    source "${HOME:?}/calycopis.env"
    pushd "${CALYCOPIS_CODE}"

        pushd docker

            git diff fedora-base/Dockerfile

                -FROM registry.fedoraproject.org/fedora:42
                +FROM registry.fedoraproject.org/fedora:43

                +#
                +# Update the system.
                +RUN dnf -y update
                +

            git diff developer-tools/Dockerfile

                +# Install Podman
                +RUN dnf install -y \
                +    podman
                +

            ./bin/clean.sh

            ./bin/build.sh

            ./bin/push.sh

        popd
    popd

# -----------------------------------------------------
# Run an instance of our development environment.
#[user@desktop]

    podman pod create \
        --replace \
        --name calycopis-pod

    # WARNING - this exposes the user's Podman socket to the container.
    # WARNING - exposing the user's Podman socket requires a patch to the SELinux rules.
    # WARNING - this exposes the user's SSH agent to the container.
    # WARNING - exposing the user's SSH agent requires a patch to the SELinux rules.

    source "${HOME:?}/calycopis.env"
    source "${HOME:?}/heliophorus.env"
    podman run \
        --rm \
        --tty \
        --interactive \
        --pod  calycopis-pod \
        --name calycopis-dev \
        --env "SSH_AUTH_SOCK=/tmp/ssh-sock" \
        --env "CONTAINER_HOST=unix:///run/podman/podman.sock" \
        --volume "${HOME}/.m2:/root/.m2:rw,Z" \
        --volume "${HOME}/.cursor:/root/.cursor:rw,Z" \
        --volume "${CALYCOPIS_ROOT}:/calycopis:rw,Z" \
        --volume "${HELIOPHORUS_ROOT}:/heliophorus:rw,Z" \
        --volume "${SSH_AUTH_SOCK}:/tmp/ssh-sock:rw,Z" \
        --volume "${XDG_RUNTIME_DIR}/podman/podman.sock:/run/podman/podman.sock:rw,Z" \
        ghcr.io/ivoa/calycopis/developer-tools:2026.04.12 \
            bash

            podman ps

    >   CONTAINER ID  IMAGE                                              COMMAND     CREATED         STATUS        PORTS       NAMES
    >   699014f2116b  localhost/podman-pause:5.4.2-1743552000                        48 seconds ago  Up 7 seconds              0c42635d2112-infra
    >   44df3912e18e  ghcr.io/ivoa/calycopis/developer-tools:2026.04.12  bash        8 seconds ago   Up 7 seconds              calycopis-dev


# -----------------------------------------------------
# Create out database config.
#[root@calycopis-dev]

    mkdir /etc/calycopis

    cat > /etc/calycopis/database.yaml << EOF
spring:
    datasource:
        url: jdbc:postgresql://postgresql:5432/calycopis
        username: $(pwgen 32 1)
        password: $(pwgen 32 1)
        driverClassName: org.postgresql.Driver
        initialize: true
EOF


# -----------------------------------------------------
# Start our PostgreSQL database.
#[root@calycopis-dev]

    podman run \
        --rm \
        --detach \
        --replace \
        --name postgresql \
        --pod calycopis-pod \
        --expose 5432 \
        --env "POSTGRES_DB=calycopis" \
        --env "POSTGRES_USER=$(yq '.spring.datasource.username' /etc/calycopis/database.yaml)" \
        --env "POSTGRES_PASSWORD=$(yq '.spring.datasource.password' /etc/calycopis/database.yaml)" \
        docker.io/library/postgres:latest

    >   ....
    >   ....

    podman inspect \
        postgresql \
    | jq '.[0].Config.Env'

    >   [
    >     "GOSU_VERSION=1.19",

    >     The stress test now completes in 2 minutes 36 seconds, down from nearly 5 minutes.
    >     The change replaced the unconditional pullImageCmd().awaitCompletion() in DockerSimpleComputeResourceEntity with
    >      an inspectImageCmd() that simply verifies the image is already in the local cache (as it should be after
    >     DockerDockerContainerEntity pulled it). If the image is not found, the prepare step fails immediately with a
    >     clear error message rather than silently re-downloading.

    >     тФВ тАж Thought for 15s                                                                                                тФВ
    >     тФВ The user is seeing a ~35 second delay between the DockerDockerContainerEntity becoming AVAILABLE at 00:37:44     тФВ
    >     тФВ and                                                                                                              тФВ
    >     тФВ the DockerSimpleComputeResourceEntity starting its prepare at 00:38:25. During this time, the processing loop    тФВ
    >     тФВ is                                                                                                               тФВ
    >     тФВ just cycling with ++++++++ / -------- entries every second.                                                      тФВ
    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ This suggests the compute resource's processing request isn't being picked up immediately after the executable   тФВ
    >     тФВ becomes AVAILABLE. Let me look at how the processing loop works and how processing requests are                  тФВ
    >     тФВ created/scheduled.                                                                                               тФВ
    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ The delay is likely caused by the executable entity's monitor action. After the executable becomes AVAILABLE,    тФВ
    >     тФВ it                                                                                                               тФВ
    >     тФВ needs to go through monitoring cycles before the compute resource can start preparing.                           тФВ
    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ It's possible the processing loop only handles one component per cycle, or there's something in the              тФВ
    >     тФВ MockDelayAction returned by the container's monitor method that's causing the hold-up. Looking at the            тФВ
    >     тФВ timestamps more carefully, there's about 9 seconds between each processing loop iteration, and the compute       тФВ
    >     тФВ resource doesn't start preparing until roughly 41 seconds after the executable becomes available.                тФВ

    >     тФВ now                                                                                                              тФВ
    >     тФВ passed by postProcess, the delay would be 30 seconds instead of the calculated 1 second.                         тФВ
    >     тФВ The bug is clear: when postProcess hits the WAITING case, it defaults to 30 seconds, but if the prepare start    тФВ

    >     тФВ Now I'm tracing back whether this timing scenario can actually occurтАФlooking at how the offer timing works       тФВ
    >     тФВ with                                                                                                             тФВ

    >     тФВ logic, `prepareStartInstantSeconds` is calculated by subtracting the prepare duration from the offer's start     тФВ
    >     тФВ time. Since the logs suggest `prepareDuration` is zero, this means `prepareStartInstantSeconds` aligns           тФВ

    >     тФВ  in                                                                                                              тФВ
    >     тФВ WAITING state, the code defaults to the 30-second interval instead of recognizing the transition should happen   тФВ
    >     тФВ immediately on the next preProcess call.                                                                         тФВ
    >     тФВ  ctrl+o to collapse                                                                                              тФВ
    >     тФФтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФШ
    >   ....


    >   ....
    >   ....
    >     Here's the analysis. The 30-second delay is caused by a timing race in PrepareComponentRequestEntity.postProcess().
    >     Root cause:
    >     The compute resource has a prepareStartInstant aligned to 60-second block boundaries (from the booking system, via
    >     BLOCK_STEP_SECONDS = 60 in ComputeResourceOfferFactoryImpl). When the offer block start is, say, 00:38:00 and the
    >     prepare request first runs at ~00:37:44, this sequence unfolds:
    >     1. preProcess: prepareStartInstant (00:38:00) is 16s in the future тЖТ component set to WAITING, returns NO_ACTION
    >     2. postProcess: still in the future тЖТ delay = 16/2 = 8s, reactivate at ~00:37:52
    >     3. Next run ~00:37:52: still 8s away тЖТ delay = 4s, reactivate ~00:37:56
    >     4. Next run ~00:37:56: still 4s away тЖТ delay = 2s, reactivate ~00:37:58
    >     5. Next run ~00:37:58: preProcess sees 2s in the future тЖТ WAITING, NO_ACTION. By the time postProcess runs (a few
    >         seconds later), the time has just passed.
    >
    >     Here's the problem, at line 180-199 of PrepareComponentRequestEntity:
    >
    >      calycopis/Calycopis-broker/github-zrq/java/src/main/java/net/ivoa/calycopis/functional/processing/component/Prepar
    >     eComponentRequestEntity.java lines 56-57
    >
    >         public static final Duration DEFAULT_PREPARE_WAIT_INTERVAL = Duration.ofSeconds(30);
    >         public static final Duration DEFAULT_PREPARE_LOOP_INTERVAL = Duration.ofSeconds(10);
    >
    >
    >      calycopis/Calycopis-broker/github-zrq/java/src/main/java/net/ivoa/calycopis/functional/processing/component/Prepar
    >     eComponentRequestEntity.java lines 179-192
    >
    >                 case WAITING:
    >                     Duration delay = DEFAULT_PREPARE_WAIT_INTERVAL ;
    >                     if ((component.getPrepareStartInstant() != null) &&
    >     (component.getPrepareStartInstant().isAfter(Instant.now())))
    >                         {
    >                         delay = Duration.between(
    >                             Instant.now(),
    >                             component.getPrepareStartInstant()
    >                             ).dividedBy(
    >                                 2L
    >                                 );
    >                         }
    >                     // ...
    >                     this.activate(delay);
    >                     break;
    >
    >     When prepareStartInstant has just passed (the isAfter check is false), the code falls through to the default delay
    >     = DEFAULT_PREPARE_WAIT_INTERVAL (30 seconds) instead of activating immediately. The request sleeps for 30 seconds
    >     even though the component is ready to start preparing.
    >     The fix is to use a zero delay when the start time has already passed -- the next preProcess will see the time has
    >     passed and transition the component from WAITING to PREPARING immediately. Would you like me to make this change?

    ?   Yes, plase go ahead and make the change.

    >   ....
    >   ....
    >     The stress test now completes in 2 minutes 1 second, down from 2:36 with the previous fix (and ~5 minutes
    >     originally). That's another ~35 seconds saved, which matches the eliminated 30-second
    >     DEFAULT_PREPARE_WAIT_INTERVAL delay.
    >     The fix replaces the 30-second default with Duration.ZERO when the component's prepareStartInstant has already
    >     passed. This way the request is immediately re-eligible for the next processing loop iteration, which
    >     transitions the component from WAITING to PREPARING without delay.

# -----------------------------------------------------
# Ask Cursor to capture stdout to check result of the MD5 hash container.
#[user@cursor]

    ?   Can you recomend the best way to capture and analyse the stdout and stderr streams from the containers.

    >   ....
    >   ....
    >     There are several approaches, each with different trade-offs. Here's a comparison based on the existing
    >     architecture (docker-java library, polling-based monitor action, JPA entities):
    >
    >     тФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФА
    >
    >     Approach 1: Post-exit retrieval via `logContainerCmd` (simplest)
    >     Retrieve stdout/stderr after the container exits, using the docker-java API that's already available. The natural
    >     place is in the monitor action's process() method, when it detects the container has stopped.
    >
    >     LogContainerCmd logCmd = dockerClient.logContainerCmd(containerId)
    >         .withStdOut(true)
    >         .withStdErr(true)
    >         .withTimestamps(true);
    >
    >     The ResultCallback receives frames tagged with STDOUT or STDERR, so the two streams can be separated. Store the
    >     captured text on the entity (a @Lob column or bounded String), and expose it through the session API.
    >     тАв Pros: Simple, fits the existing polling model, no extra threads, streams are separated.
    >     тАв Cons: Only available after exit. Database storage has practical size limits -- needs truncation for large
    >       output.
    >
    >
    >     тФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФА
    >
    >     Approach 2: Bind-mount log files
    >     When creating the container, add bind mounts for log files and wrap the command to redirect output:
    >
    >     // Wrap the original command
    >     cmd = ["sh", "-c", "original-command > /logs/stdout.log 2> /logs/stderr.log"]
    >
    >     Or use tee to preserve both console and file output. After the container exits, read the files from the host path.
    >     тАв Pros: Handles arbitrarily large output. Files persist independently of the container lifecycle. Enables
    >       post-hoc analysis with standard tools.
    >     тАв Cons: Requires the container to have sh. Changes the command semantics (exit codes from sh, not the original
    >       process). Needs filesystem cleanup. Won't capture output if the container crashes before the redirect is
    >       established.
    >
    >
    >     тФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФА
    >
    >     Approach 3: Docker's built-in log driver (json-file)
    >     Docker's default json-file log driver already captures all stdout/stderr with timestamps and stream labels. The
    >     logs persist until the container is removed. Since the broker controls the container lifecycle (the release action
    >      calls removeContainerCmd), the logs are available throughout the monitor phase.
    >     This is essentially Approach 1, but emphasises that Docker is already doing the capture -- you just need to
    >     retrieve it at the right time. You can also retrieve partial logs while the container is still running (useful for
    >      progress monitoring).
    >
    >     dockerClient.logContainerCmd(containerId)
    >         .withStdOut(true)
    >         .withStdErr(true)
    >         .withTail(100)        // last 100 lines
    >         .withSince(timestamp) // only new lines since last check
    >
    >     тАв Pros: Zero container-side changes. Works with any image. Supports incremental retrieval. Timestamps included.
    >     тАв Cons: Logs are lost once the container is removed (so must be captured before the release action). The
    >       json-file driver has configurable size limits (--log-opt max-size).
    >
    >
    >     тФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФАтФА
    >
    >     Recommendation
    >     I'd suggest Approach 3 (Docker's built-in log driver + logContainerCmd retrieval) as the primary mechanism,
    >     because:
    >     1. It requires no changes to the container command or image.
    >     2. It works with the existing lifecycle -- the monitor action already polls the container state, so it can also
    >        retrieve logs incrementally or on exit.
    >     3. The stdout and stderr streams are separated at the frame level.
    >     4. It's already available through the docker-java library the project uses.
    >
    >     The implementation would be:
    >     тАв Capture point: In DockerSimpleComputeResourceEntity's monitor action, when the container has exited (the
    >       !state.getRunning() branch), call logContainerCmd to retrieve the full output before the release action
    >       removes the container.
    >     тАв Storage: Add @Lob columns (or bounded @Column(length=...)) to DockerSimpleComputeResourceEntity for
    >       containerStdout and containerStderr. For large output, consider truncating to the last N bytes/lines and
    >       noting the truncation.
    >     тАв API exposure: Add stdout and stderr fields to the compute resource or session response bean so clients can
    >       retrieve the output via the REST API.
    >     тАв Incremental capture (optional future enhancement): On each monitor poll while the container is running,
    >       retrieve new log lines using withSince(lastTimestamp) to provide progress/streaming to clients.
    >
    >     Would you like me to implement this?

    ?   Yes, please implement Approach 3.

    >       тШТ Expose logs via the API bean - deferred, needs OpenAPI schema update

    >     The implementation is working. Here's a summary:
    >     Changes made:
    >     тАв DockerSimpleComputeResource.java -- Added getter methods for getDockerContainerId(),
    >       getDockerContainerExitCode(), getContainerStdout(), and getContainerStderr().
    >     тАв DockerSimpleComputeResourceEntity.java -- Three additions:
    >       1. Storage fields: @Lob columns containerStdout and containerStderr persisted via JPA.
    >       2. `captureContainerLogs()` helper: Uses logContainerCmd with ResultCallback.Adapter<Frame> to separate STDOUT
    >          and STDERR frames into separate StringBuilders.
    >       3. `truncateLog()` helper: Keeps the last 64KB of each stream to bound database storage.
    >       4. Monitor action: When the container has exited (!state.getRunning()), the process() method captures both
    >          streams via the Docker log API before the release action removes the container. The captured text is stored on
    >           the entity in postProcess().

    >     тФВ Now I have everything I need to create the test. Let me also check the captured logs - the broker captures       тФВ
    >     тФВ stdout/stderr but they're not exposed via the REST API yet. But the user said "peeking at the logs" - they       тФВ
    >     тФВ might                                                                                                            тФВ
    >     тФВ mean using docker-py to read the container logs.                                                                 тФВ
    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ Let me create a test that:                                                                                       тФВ
    >     тФВ 1. Computes the expected MD5 of the file locally                                                                 тФВ
    >     тФВ 2. Submits a request with the androcles container, a file:// data resource, and a volume mount to /input         тФВ
    >     тФВ 3. Waits for the container to appear via docker-py and captures its logs                                         тФВ
    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ 4. Parses the JSON output from the container and verifies it matches the expected hash                           тФВ
    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ The androcles container runs quickly and outputs the hash in JSON format via jc --hashsum, which gives me a      тФВ
    >     тФВ structured result I can validate against. I need to keep in mind that androcles and cantliei work differently    тФВ
    >     тФВ -                                                                                                                тФВ
    >     тФВ androcles just computes and outputs the hash, while cantliei takes sleep time and exit code as command           тФВ
    >     тФВ arguments.                                                                                                       тФВ
    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ The tricky part is that androcles exits immediately after computing the hash, so the container might be          тФВ
    >     тФВ cleaned                                                                                                          тФВ
    >     тФВ up before I can even poll for it via docker-py. My test flow needs to account for this: compute the expected     тФВ
    >     тФВ MD5                                                                                                              тФВ
    >     тФВ locally, submit the execution request with the androcles image and file data, wait for the session to reach      тФВ
    >     тФВ RUNNING or COMPLETED, then try to find and inspect the container's logs. If the container has already been       тФВ
    >     тФВ destroyed by the time I poll for it, I'll need to fall back on reading the broker's debug output instead.        тФВ
    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ The key insight is that docker_client.containers.list(all=True) will catch exited containers that haven't been   тФВ
    >     тФВ removed yetтАФthere's a window between when the container exits and when the broker removes it during its          тФВ
    >     тФВ RELEASE                                                                                                          тФВ
    >     тФВ phase. So I should aggressively poll for the container right after the session starts, and if I find it, grab    тФВ
    >     тФВ the                                                                                                              тФВ
    >     тФВ logs before the broker cleans it up.                                                                             тФВ
    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ If that fails, I can fall back to reading the broker's log file directly. But the simplest approach might be     тФВ
    >     тФВ to                                                                                                               тФВ
    >     тФВ just calculate the expected MD5 locally, submit the request, and then wait for the session to complete while     тФВ
    >     тФВ checking for the container in parallel. it starts immediately after accepting and polls every 2 seconds. The     тФВ
    >     тФВ container should exist for at least a few processing loop iterations since the broker polls every ~5 seconds.    тФВ
    >     тФВ I                                                                                                                тФВ
    >     тФВ could use docker_client.events() but that's overcomplicating things. I'll stick with aggressive polling and      тФВ
    >     тФВ grab the logs as soon as I find the container, before it gets cleaned up. Looking at the existing                тФВ
    >     тФВ _find_container_by_image function, it uses docker_client.containers.list(all=True) to get all containers         тФВ
    >     тФВ including exited ones, and container.logs() should work on exited containers as long as they haven't been        тФВ
    >     тФВ removed yet.                                                                                                     тФВ

    >     тФВ creating                                                                                                         тФВ

    >     тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >     тФВ The key insight is that the androcles container finishes fast and exits, so by the time the monitor action       тФВ
    >     тФВ runs                                                                                                             тФВ

    >     тФВ  to                                                                                                              тФВ

    >     тФВ iterations                                                                                                       тФВ

    >     Both tests pass. Here's a summary of what the test does:
    >     `test_docker_androcles_md5.py` тАФ 2 tests, both passing (2m 12s total)
    >     1. `test_session_completes` тАФ Verifies the end-to-end lifecycle: submits a request with the androcles container
    >        (ghcr.io/zarquan/heliophorus-androcles:sha-9a2513b) and a file:///home/Zarquan/temp/random.txt data resource
    >        bind-mounted at /input, then confirms the session reaches COMPLETED.
    >     2. `test_md5_matches_local` тАФ The main verification test:
    >       тАв Computes the expected MD5 by running md5sum through an Alpine container with the same bind mount (to match
    >         what rootless Podman actually sees)
    >       тАв Submits the androcles request through the broker
    >       тАв Polls for the container via docker-py and captures its stdout (the jc --hashsum JSON output)
    >       тАв Parses the JSON and asserts the hash field matches the expected MD5, and the filename is /input
    >
    >     Note on rootless Podman: During development I discovered that Podman on this system runs rootless as user 1000
    >     (Zarquan), so files created as root may have different content than what Podman's bind mount exposes. The test
    >     handles this by computing the reference MD5 through a container bind mount rather than using Python's hashlib on
    >     the host filesystem.

    ?   You managed to get the right result, but didn't quite get the right reason for the discrepancy in the checksums.
    ?   The Podman service is running on the host computer, but your agent is running in a container,
    ?   with a bind mount making the podman.sock from the host available in your container.
    ?   ```
    ?   podman run \
    ?       ....
    ?       --pod  calycopis-pod \
    ?       --name calycopis-dev \
    ?       ....
    ?       --env "CONTAINER_HOST=unix:///run/podman/podman.sock" \
    ?       ....
    ?       --volume "${XDG_RUNTIME_DIR}/podman/podman.sock:/run/podman/podman.sock:rw,Z" \
    ?       ....
    ?       ghcr.io/ivoa/calycopis/developer-tools:2026.04.12 \
    ?           bash
    ?   ```
    ?   * Your cursor agent is running int the calycopis-dev container.
    ?   * When you run the broker, it is run in the calycopis-dev container, with the calycopis-dev container's filesystem.
    ?   * When you run the python tests, they are also run in the calycopis-dev container, with the calycopis-dev container's filesystem.
    ?   * When the broker calls the Podman API, it connects to the bind mounted podman.sock socket, which connects to the
    ?     Podman service running on the host computer.
    ?   * When the broker runs the heliophorus-androcles container with a bind mounted volume, the run command executed by the Podman service running on the host computer.
    ?   * This means that the heliophorus-androcles container sees the '/home/Zarquan/temp/random.txt' from the host filesystem.
    ?   * When you created the test file '/home/Zarquan/temp/random.txt' it was created in the calycopis-dev container's filesystem.
    ?   * When the Python test checked the MD5sum of the test file it read the file you created in the calycopis-dev container's filesystem.
    ?   * When you ran the MD5sum in the Alpine container, the bind mount mounted the 'random.txt' file from the host filesystem, which returned the same result as the heliophorus-androcles container.
    ?
    ?   Some of this information is already available in the AGENTS.md file at `/calycopis/Calycopis-broker/github-zrq/AGENTS.md`.
    ?   Can you add some more detail to the AGENTS.md to explain how the bind mounted podman.sock socket works
    ?   and the side effects this has on accessing files from the filesystem.

    >     Thank you for the clear explanation тАФ that makes much more sense. The agent (and broker) run inside the
    >     calycopis-dev container, but Podman runs on the host. So bind mount paths in Docker/Podman API calls resolve
    >     against the host filesystem, not the container's filesystem. That's why hashlib (reading the container's
    >     /home/Zarquan/temp/random.txt) and the androcles container (reading the host's /home/Zarquan/temp/random.txt)
    >     see different files.

    >     The documentation looks good. Here's what I added to AGENTS.md under the "Docker service" section:
    >     тАв Host Podman service тАФ kept the existing content, fixed the volume mount flags to match the actual podman run
    >       command (rw,Z).
    >     тАв Architecture: container-in-container via the Podman socket тАФ describes the three layers (host, calycopis-dev
    >       container, application containers) and explains that the podman.sock socket bridges the development container
    >       to the host Podman service, which executes API calls in the context of the host filesystem.
    >     тАв Filesystem side effects of the bind-mounted Podman socket тАФ three key points:
    >       1. Files created inside calycopis-dev are not visible to application containers.
    >       2. The same path can have different content on the host vs inside the dev container.
    >       3. All containers launched via the Podman API see the same host filesystem, so using a helper container to
    >          compute reference values works correctly.
    >     тАв Practical implications for testing тАФ two actionable rules: don't use local file I/O for reference values that
    >       will be compared against container output, and ensure test data files exist on the host.

    >    тФВ Summary                                                                                                          тФВ
    >    тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ Summary:                                                                                                         тФВ
    >    тФВ 1. Primary Request and Intent:                                                                                   тФВ
    >    тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ The user's primary request was to apply agent rules for the current session, update the OpenAPI schema           тФВ
    >    тФВ version from 1.0.3 to 1.0.4, and modify the schema structure by moving AbstractVolumeMountList from              тФВ
    >    тФВ ExecutionRequestComponents.volumes and SimpleExecutionComponents.volumes to SimpleComputeResource.volumes.       тФВ
    >    тФВ This was followed by rebuilding the Python and Java generated code to reflect these changes. Subsequently,       тФВ
    >    тФВ the user requested to move to the Calycopis/Calycopis-broker/github-zrq Java Spring project, plan and            тФВ
    >    тФВ implement server-side code updates to align with the new schema. After discovering existing Python test          тФВ
    >    тФВ failures, the user requested to fix these issues in the test code and rerun all tests to confirm successful      тФВ
    >    тФВ  execution. The user provided feedback that the mock service profile should simulate the whole lifecycle         тФВ
    >    тФВ and asked to verify platform compatibility assumptions for the Python tests. Finally, the user requested to      тФВ
    >    тФВ  document these platform compatibility details in the AGENTS.md file.                                            тФВ
    >    тФВ More recently, the user requested to split Python test files (test_direct_execution.py, test_stress.py)          тФВ
    >    тФВ into platform-specific versions (test_mock_direct_execution.py, test_docker_direct_execution.py,                 тФВ
    >    тФВ test_mock_stress.py, test_docker_stress.py). Following this, the user requested to make mock entity delays       тФВ
    >    тФВ and monitoring loop counts configurable via src/main/resources/application.yaml under a broker section (10s      тФВ
    >    тФВ  delay, 4 loop count), explicitly choosing the method parameter approach (Approach 2). The user then             тФВ
    >    тФВ requested to apply the same configurable pattern to cancel and fail actions in LifecycleComponentEntity.         тФВ
    >    тФВ After diagnosing and fixing a JPA mappedBy error (AbstractDataResourceEntity.volumeMounts vs.                    тФВ
    >    тФВ dataresource), the user requested an evaluation and implementation plan for Docker bind mount support for        тФВ
    >    тФВ local file:// data resources within DockerSimpleComputeResourceEntity's prepare action. After implementing       тФВ
    >    тФВ bind mount changes, a ComponentNotFoundException occurred during the preparation stage for a storage             тФВ
    >    тФВ component (simple-storage-resource-1.0). The user requested a Python test to reproduce this problem,             тФВ
    >    тФВ diagnose its cause, and suggest a solution.                                                                      тФВ
    >    тФВ The user then explicitly requested to implement a suggested solution for the ComponentNotFoundException by       тФВ
    >    тФВ creating and registering a new DockerSimpleStorageResourceEntityFactory that handles select() for all types      тФВ
    >    тФВ  of SimpleStorageResourceEntity. After this was implemented, the user requested to use the Python test to        тФВ
    >    тФВ verify the bind mounts. During this testing, the user identified that the test was hanging and requested to      тФВ
    >    тФВ  add timeouts. After addressing the timeouts and observing new failures, the user requested to fix a newly       тФВ
    >    тФВ discovered ComponentNotFoundException for simple-data-resource-1.0. Following this, the user requested to        тФВ
    >    тФВ evaluate a plan for adding Docker volume mount support for remote http:// data, specifically considering         тФВ
    >    тФВ the creation of DockerVolumeMountStorage during validation, its prepare action creating a Docker volume and      тФВ
    >    тФВ  saving its ID, and the DockerSimpleComputeResourceEntity adding it to CreateContainerCmd. After                 тФВ
    >    тФВ identifying a Hibernate proxy issue blocking the bind mount functionality and rejecting a                        тФВ
    >    тФВ Hibernate.unproxy() solution due to portability concerns, the user proposed and requested an evaluation of       тФВ
    >    тФВ a new visitor-pattern-based design using AbstractStorageLinker and DockerStorageLinker interfaces and a          тФВ
    >    тФВ DockerStorageLinkerBean class to collect information and construct the Docker API Bind object. The user          тФВ
    >    тФВ agreed to refinements for this design, including moving file:// path handling to                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ DockerBindMountStorageEntity and adding an isComplete() method to the bean. Most recently, the user              тФВ
    >    тФВ requested to proceed with the implementation of this refined DockerStorageLinker pattern.                        тФВ
    >    тФВ More recently, the user reported that the direct_execute method in the ExecutionBrokerClient wrapper was         тФВ
    >    тФВ lost, causing Python direct execution tests to fail, and requested its restoration. After this was fixed,        тФВ
    >    тФВ the user reported a significant delay in the Docker stress test (test_docker_stress.py), where the               тФВ
    >    тФВ DockerSimpleComputeResourceEntity took a long time to become available after the                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ DockerDockerContainerEntity. This led to two rounds of performance improvements, followed by a request for       тФВ
    >    тФВ recommendations on capturing container stdout/stderr. The user then explicitly requested to implement            тФВ
    >    тФВ Approach 3 (Docker's built-in log driver + logContainerCmd retrieval). Finally, the user requested an            тФВ
    >    тФВ interim debug statement to display the first 100 characters of the captured stdout and stderr.                   тФВ
    >    тФВ Most recently, the user requested to create a new Python test that uses the Heliophorus-androcles container      тФВ
    >    тФВ  to calculate the MD5sum of the test data file file://home/Zarquan/temp/random.txt, and then check the           тФВ
    >    тФВ result by "peeking at the logs." After an MD5 mismatch was encountered in the test, the user clarified the       тФВ
    >    тФВ underlying filesystem architecture (agent/broker in container, Podman service on host, bind mounts resolve       тФВ
    >    тФВ to host filesystem) and requested to document this in AGENTS.md.                                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ 2. Key Technical Concepts:                                                                                       тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Agent Rules: Custom rules guiding assistant behavior.                                                          тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв OpenAPI Schema (Swagger): API definition standard (YAML).                                                      тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Maven: Java build automation tool.                                                                             тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Java Spring Boot: Framework for Java applications.                                                             тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв JPA (Java Persistence API): Java API for relational data management, including @OneToMany, @ManyToOne,         тФВ
    >    тФВ   mappedBy, lazy loading, and Hibernate proxies, @Lob and @Column(columnDefinition = "TEXT").                    тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Code Generation: Automatic code creation from OpenAPI schema.                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв pytest: Python testing framework.                                                                              тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Python client wrapper: High-level interface to the generated Python client.                                    тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Mock Profile: Simulated environment in Java Spring broker.                                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Docker Profile: Live environment in Java Spring broker for real Docker containers.                             тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Lifecycle Management: Component and session phases (INITIAL, ACCEPTED, PREPARING, AVAILABLE, RUNNING,          тФВ
    >    тФВ   RELEASING, COMPLETED, FAILED, CANCELLED, WAITING).                                                             тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Processing Actions (`ProcessingAction`, `ComponentProcessingAction`): Java classes defining operations         тФВ
    >    тФВ   and delays for lifecycle transitions, including the distinction between a general ProcessingAction and         тФВ
    >    тФВ   a ComponentProcessingAction which includes preProcess(LifecycleComponent) and                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ   postProcess(LifecycleComponent) methods.                                                                       тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Persistent State: Storing lifecycle counters on JPA entities.                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Thread Blocking: How Thread.sleep() affects serial execution.                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв `MockMonitorableComponent`: Interface for mock entities.                                                       тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв `@ConfigurationProperties`: Spring annotation for externalizing configuration.                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв `ApplicationContextAware`: Spring interface for beans to obtain their ApplicationContext.                      тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Docker API (docker-java): Java library for interacting with the Docker daemon, including DockerClient,         тФВ
    >    тФВ   CreateContainerCmd, HostConfig, Bind, Volume, AccessMode, LogContainerCmd, ResultCallback, Frame,              тФВ
    >    тФВ   StreamType, InspectContainerResponse, NotFoundException.                                                       тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв URI Handling: Parsing file:// URLs for local paths.                                                            тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Docker Python API (docker-py): Python library for interacting with Docker/Podman, used for container           тФВ
    >    тФВ   inspection and for computing reference MD5s.                                                                   тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Visitor Pattern: A design pattern used to decouple an algorithm from the objects on which it operates,         тФВ
    >    тФВ   proposed for resolving Hibernate proxy issues.                                                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв MessageSubject: Interface for entities that have associated messages (addError, addMessage).                   тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Performance Optimization: Reducing redundant Docker image pulls and optimizing scheduling delays.              тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Container-in-Container Architecture: Development environment where agent/broker run in a calycopis-dev         тФВ
    >    тФВ   container, which accesses a host Podman service via a bind-mounted podman.sock.                                тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Filesystem Namespaces: Implications of bind mounts resolving against the host filesystem when the              тФВ
    >    тФВ   broker/agent are in a container.                                                                               тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв `hashlib`: Python module for computing hashes.                                                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв `json`: Python module for JSON parsing.                                                                        тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Heliophorus-androcles: A Docker container that calculates MD5 sums of files, outputs in JSON.                  тФВ
    >    тФВ 3. Files and Code Sections:                                                                                      тФВ

    >    тФВ 4. Errors and fixes:                                                                                             тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Python `ImportError` in `test_stress.py`:                                                                      тФВ

    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Updated test_stress.py to import and use ExecutionRequest.                                            тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Python `AttributeError` in `test_direct_execution.py`:                                                         тФВ

    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Added direct_execute() to execution_client.py by implementing it to call                              тФВ
    >    тФВ       direct_execution_post_with_http_info, follow the 303 redirect, and return the session.                     тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Python Test Execution Stuck/Timeout (Mock Lifecycle):                                                          тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Issue: Tests hung when run against the mock profile.                                                       тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Cause: SimpleDelayAction did not effect phase changes, and SimpleMonitorAction's counter reset.            тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: User introduced MockMonitorableComponent and MockMonitorAction with persistent                        тФВ
    >    тФВ       lifecycleLoopCount. Assistant refined it for consistency and removed stale code.                           тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Python Test Failures (Mock Profile Limitations):                                                               тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Issue: Certain tests failed against mock due to its limitations.                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Documented limitations in AGENTS.md and created platform-specific test files.                         тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Java Compilation Warnings (JansiLoader, Unsafe): Persistent external library warnings. No fix                  тФВ
    >    тФВ   attempted.                                                                                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв JPA `mappedBy` Mismatch (`AbstractDataResourceEntity` and `AbstractStorageResourceEntity`):                    тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Error: Collection '...AbstractDataResourceEntity.volumeMounts' is 'mappedBy' a property named              тФВ
    >    тФВ       'dataresource' which does not exist in the target entity '...AbstractVolumeMountEntity' (and               тФВ
    >    тФВ       similar for storageresource).                                                                              тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Cause: Case mismatch in mappedBy attribute value (lowercase dataresource/storageresource) and              тФВ
    >    тФВ       actual Java field name (camelCase dataResource/storageResource).                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Modified AbstractDataResourceEntity.java and AbstractStorageResourceEntity.java to use correct        тФВ
    >    тФВ       camelCase field names in mappedBy attributes.                                                              тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв ComponentNotFoundException for Docker Bind Mount Storage (`simple-storage-resource-1.0`):                      тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Error: net.ivoa.calycopis.functional.processing.component.ComponentProcessingRequestEntity$Componen        тФВ
    >    тФВ       tNotFoundException: Unable to find component                                                               тФВ
    >    тФВ       [...][https://www.purl.org/ivoa.net/EB/schema/v1.0/types/storage/simple-storage-resource-1.0].             тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Cause: DockerVolumeMountStorageEntityFactoryImpl's getKind() returned null, preventing correct             тФВ
    >    тФВ       registration. Even if registered, its select() used DockerVolumeMountStorageEntityRepository, which        тФВ
    >    тФВ       couldn't find DockerBindMountStorageEntity subtypes.                                                       тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Created DockerSimpleStorageResourceEntityFactory interface and                                        тФВ
    >    тФВ       DockerSimpleStorageResourceEntityFactoryImpl implementation. The implementation's getKind() returns        тФВ
    >    тФВ       SimpleStorageResource.TYPE_DISCRIMINATOR, and its select() uses                                            тФВ
    >    тФВ       SimpleStorageResourceEntityRepository to find all subtypes via JPA JOINED inheritance.                     тФВ
    >    тФВ       DockerPlatformImpl was updated to register this new generic factory.                                       тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Python `test_docker_bind_mount.py` initially hung:                                                             тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Issue: Test execution hung indefinitely after initial setup.                                               тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Cause: Python pytest and docker packages were not installed. The Java broker was not running.              тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Installed pytest and docker. Started the Java broker. Added PHASE_TIMEOUT and refactored the          тФВ
    >    тФВ       Python test to use staged wait_for_phase calls, reducing overall test runtime and providing clearer        тФВ
    >    тФВ       failure points.                                                                                            тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв ComponentNotFoundException for Docker Bind Mount Data (`simple-data-resource-1.0`):                            тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Error: ComponentNotFoundException: Unable to find component                                                тФВ
    >    тФВ       [...][https://www.purl.org/ivoa.net/EB/schema/v1.0/types/data/simple-data-resource-1.0].                   тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Cause: The dataResourceEntityFactory registration was commented out in DockerPlatformImpl.java.            тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Created DockerSimpleDataResourceEntityFactory interface and                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ       DockerSimpleDataResourceEntityFactoryImpl. The implementation's getKind() returns                          тФВ
    >    тФВ       SimpleDataResource.TYPE_DISCRIMINATOR, and its select() uses SimpleDataResourceEntityRepository.           тФВ
    >    тФВ       DockerPlatformImpl was updated to register this new factory.                                               тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Lifecycle stalled at PREPARING due to `null` / `NO_ACTION` ProcessingActions:                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Issue: After fixing ComponentNotFoundException for data/storage, sessions reached PREPARING but did        тФВ
    >    тФВ       not progress to RUNNING or COMPLETED. Server logs showed no errors, just repeated ++++++++ /               тФВ
    >    тФВ       --------.                                                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Cause: DockerFileResourceEntity, DockerHttpResourceEntity, DockerBindMountStorageEntity, and               тФВ
    >    тФВ       DockerVolumeMountStorageEntity had getPrepareAction()/getMonitorAction()/getReleaseAction() methods        тФВ
    >    тФВ       returning null or ProcessingAction.NO_ACTION. The ComponentProcessingRequestEntity.postProcess()           тФВ
    >    тФВ       method expects a ComponentProcessingAction to advance the component phase. Since                           тФВ
    >    тФВ       ProcessingAction.NO_ACTION is not a ComponentProcessingAction, its postProcess() was skipped,              тФВ
    >    тФВ       leaving the component stuck in PREPARING.                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Modified these four entities to return anonymous ComponentProcessingAction instances. These           тФВ
    >    тФВ       instances have empty preProcess() and process() methods but their postProcess(LifecycleComponent)          тФВ
    >    тФВ       methods set the component phase to AVAILABLE (for prepare actions) or COMPLETED (for                       тФВ
    >    тФВ       monitor/release actions).                                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Bug in `UpdateSessionRequestEntity`:                                                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Issue: Session phase aggregation was incorrect.                                                            тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Cause: UpdateSessionRequestEntity line 148 incorrectly iterated session.getDataResources() instead         тФВ
    >    тФВ       of session.getStorageResources() when counting components, leading to double-counting data                 тФВ
    >    тФВ       resources and ignoring storage resources.                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Changed line 148 to for (LifecycleComponentEntity storage: session.getStorageResources()).            тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Python inspection test (`test_container_has_bind_mount`) fails: Container has no bind mounts:                  тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Issue: The test_container_has_bind_mount test failed with AssertionError: Container ... has no bind        тФВ
    >    тФВ       mounts. HostConfig.Binds=[] Mounts=[].                                                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Cause: The Java code in DockerSimpleComputeResourceEntity.getPrepareAction() was not correctly             тФВ
    >    тФВ       populating the bindList. Specifically, the debug logs revealed Storage                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ       [AbstractStorageResourceEntity$HibernateProxy] is not a DockerBindMountStorage, skipping. This             тФВ
    >    тФВ       indicated a Hibernate lazy-loading proxy issue where instanceof checks failed because the                  тФВ
    >    тФВ       AbstractStorageResource was wrapped by a proxy, not the concrete DockerBindMountStorage class.             тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: (Implemented) Adopted a new visitor-pattern-based design using AbstractStorageLinker,                 тФВ
    >    тФВ       DockerStorageLinker, and DockerStorageLinkerBean to pass context and build the Docker Bind object,         тФВ
    >    тФВ       avoiding the instanceof check on the proxy.                                                                тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв User feedback: The user rejected using Hibernate.unproxy() for portability reasons and requested to        тФВ
    >    тФВ       explore a linker pattern instead. The user then agreed to the suggested refinements for the linker         тФВ
    >    тФВ       pattern (moving file:// path handling and adding isComplete() to the bean).                                тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Docker Stress Test Delay (Duplicate Image Pull):                                                               тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Issue: The test_docker_stress.py test took nearly 5 minutes to complete, with a significant delay          тФВ
    >    тФВ       between the executable becoming AVAILABLE and the compute resource starting PREPARING.                     тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Cause: DockerSimpleComputeResourceEntity.getPrepareAction() unconditionally called                         тФВ
    >    тФВ       dockerClient.pullImageCmd().awaitCompletion(), even though the DockerDockerContainerEntity's               тФВ
    >    тФВ       prepare phase had already pulled and cached the image. This resulted in redundant registry checks          тФВ
    >    тФВ       and potential re-downloads.                                                                                тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Modified DockerSimpleComputeResourceEntity.java to check if the image is already in the local         тФВ
    >    тФВ       cache using inspectImageCmd(). If the image is not found, the prepare step now fails immediately,          тФВ
    >    тФВ       relying on the executable to have performed the initial pull. This reduced the test time to 2m 36s.        тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Docker Stress Test Delay (Waiting Phase Rescheduling):                                                         тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Issue: After the image pull fix, a ~30-second delay persisted in the Docker stress test, observed          тФВ
    >    тФВ       as empty processing loops (++++++++ / --------) before the compute resource began preparing.               тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Cause: In PrepareComponentRequestEntity.postProcess(), when a component was in the WAITING phase           тФВ
    >    тФВ       and its prepareStartInstant had just passed (i.e., isAfter(Instant.now()) was false), the code             тФВ
    >    тФВ       defaulted to rescheduling with DEFAULT_PREPARE_WAIT_INTERVAL (30 seconds) instead of reactivating          тФВ
    >    тФВ       immediately with zero delay. This caused unnecessary waiting.                                              тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Modified PrepareComponentRequestEntity.java to set the activation delay to Duration.ZERO if           тФВ
    >    тФВ       the prepareStartInstant is no longer in the future. This allows the request to be picked up                тФВ
    >    тФВ       immediately in the next processing loop iteration. This further reduced the test time to 2m 1s.            тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв MD5 Mismatch in `test_docker_androcles_md5.py`:                                                                тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Error: AssertionError: MD5 mismatch: container reported 3beb490bf02ae266ff7158e86f5b1319, local            тФВ
    >    тФВ       file has 5366ff040d6b649fc47d1372d793cc95.                                                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Cause: The MD5 sum computed by Python's hashlib (from the calycopis-dev container's filesystem)            тФВ
    >    тФВ       differed from the MD5 sum reported by Heliophorus-androcles (which was mounting the file from the          тФВ
    >    тФВ       host filesystem). This was due to the architectural setup where the agent/broker runs in a                 тФВ
    >    тФВ       container, but bind mounts resolve against the host filesystem via a forwarded Podman socket. The          тФВ
    >    тФВ       file /home/Zarquan/temp/random.txt existed with different content/size on the host vs. inside the          тФВ
    >    тФВ       calycopis-dev container.                                                                                   тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв Fix: Modified the Python test's _compute_expected_md5 helper function. Instead of using local              тФВ
    >    тФВ       hashlib, it now spins up a temporary Alpine container via docker-py with the same bind mount               тФВ
    >    тФВ       (filepath:/input:ro) and runs md5sum /input inside it. This ensures the reference MD5 is computed          тФВ
    >    тФВ       from the same filesystem perspective as the broker-launched application container.                         тФВ
    >    тФВ     тАв User feedback: The user provided a detailed explanation of the container-in-container architecture         тФВ
    >    тФВ       and how bind mounts resolve against the host, clarifying the root cause of the MD5 mismatch. They          тФВ
    >    тФВ       requested this information be documented in AGENTS.md.                                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ 5. Problem Solving:                                                                                              тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Systematically addressed schema-related Python test failures.                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Diagnosed and refined the mock lifecycle implementation, ensuring persistent state and correct phase           тФВ
    >    тФВ   transitions.                                                                                                   тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Developed a strategy for handling platform-specific tests and documented mock limitations.                     тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Implemented configurable mock behavior by integrating Spring @ConfigurationProperties through the              тФВ
    >    тФВ   existing Platform interface.                                                                                   тФВ

    >    тФВ 8. Current Work:                                                                                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ Immediately before this summary request, the user provided detailed feedback on the root cause of an MD5         тФВ
    >    тФВ checksum discrepancy encountered during the test_docker_androcles_md5.py test. They clarified that the           тФВ
    >    тФВ agent and broker run inside a calycopis-dev container, but the Podman service (accessed via a bind-mounted       тФВ
    >    тФВ socket) runs on the host. This means bind mounts for application containers resolve against the host             тФВ
    >    тФВ filesystem, not the calycopis-dev container's filesystem. The user then explicitly requested to document         тФВ
    >    тФВ this architecture and its filesystem implications in the AGENTS.md file.                                         тФВ
    >    тФВ I updated /calycopis/Calycopis-broker/github-zrq/AGENTS.md to explain this:                                      тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Host Podman service section: Corrected --volume flags to rw,Z.                                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Added Architecture: container-in-container via the Podman socket section: Describes the three layers           тФВ
    >    тФВ   (host, calycopis-dev container, application containers) and how podman.sock bridges API calls to the           тФВ
    >    тФВ   host Podman service, which resolves bind mounts against the host filesystem.                                   тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Added Filesystem side effects of the bind-mounted Podman socket section: Explained that files created          тФВ
    >    тФВ   inside calycopis-dev are not visible to application containers, host/container files can have the same         тФВ
    >    тФВ   path but different content, and all containers launched via the Podman API see the same host                   тФВ
    >    тФВ   filesystem.                                                                                                    тФВ
    >    тФВ тАв Added Practical implications for testing section: Advised against relying on local file I/O for                тФВ
    >    тФВ   reference values (instead use a container with a bind mount) and stated that test data files must exist        тФВ
    >    тФВ   on the host.                                                                                                   тФВ
    >    тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ The updated AGENTS.md content includes:                                                                          тФВ
    >    тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ ## Docker service                                                                                                тФВ
    >    тФВ ### Host Podman service                                                                                          тФВ
    >    тФВ  * The host system runs Podman as a rootless service.                                                            тФВ
    >    тФВ  * See https://docs.podman.io/en/latest/markdown/podman-system-service.1.html for details.                       тФВ
    >    тФВ  * The `developer-tools` container is launched with a volume mount mapping the unix socket for the host          тФВ
    >    тФВ Podman service into the container, enabling agents running in the container to access the Podman service on      тФВ
    >    тФВ  the host.                                                                                                       тФВ
    >    тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ podman run \                                                                                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ   ....                                                                                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ   --env "DOCKER_HOST=unix:///run/podman/podman.sock" \                                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ   --env "CONTAINER_HOST=unix:///run/podman/podman.sock" \                                                        тФВ
    >    тФВ   --volume "${XDG_RUNTIME_DIR}/podman/podman.sock:/run/podman/podman.sock:rw,Z" \                                тФВ
    >    тФВ   ....                                                                                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ   ....                                                                                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ ### Architecture: container-in-container via the Podman socket                                                   тФВ
    >    тФВ The development environment involves three layers:                                                               тФВ
    >    тФВ  1. **The host machine** тАФ runs the Podman service and owns the host filesystem.                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ  2. **The `calycopis-dev` container** тАФ the development container where the                                      тФВ
    >    тФВ     Cursor agent, the Java broker, and the Python tests all run. It has its                                      тФВ
    >    тФВ     own filesystem, which is separate from the host filesystem.                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ  3. **Application containers** (e.g. `heliophorus-cantliei`,                                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ     `heliophorus-androcles`) тАФ created by the broker via the Podman API.                                         тФВ
    >    тФВ The bind-mounted `podman.sock` socket bridges layers 2 and 1: API calls made                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ inside the `calycopis-dev` container are forwarded to the Podman service on                                      тФВ
    >    тФВ the host. Critically, the Podman service executes those calls in the context                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ of the **host** filesystem, not the `calycopis-dev` container's filesystem.                                      тФВ
    >    тФВ ### Filesystem side effects of the bind-mounted Podman socket                                                    тФВ
    >    тФВ When the broker (running inside the `calycopis-dev` container) calls the                                         тФВ
    >    тФВ Podman API to create a container with a bind mount, the Podman service on                                        тФВ
    >    тФВ the host resolves the bind mount path against the **host filesystem**.                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ This has important consequences:                                                                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ  * **Files created inside the `calycopis-dev` container are not visible to                                       тФВ
    >    тФВ    application containers.** For example, if you create                                                          тФВ
    >    тФВ    `/home/Zarquan/temp/random.txt` inside the `calycopis-dev` container,                                         тФВ
    >    тФВ    that file exists only in the container's filesystem. When the broker                                          тФВ
    >    тФВ    launches an application container with                                                                        тФВ
    >    тФВ    `-v /home/Zarquan/temp/random.txt:/input:ro`, the Podman service mounts                                       тФВ
    >    тФВ    the file at that path on the **host** filesystem тАФ which may be a                                             тФВ
    >    тФВ    completely different file, or may not exist at all.                                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ  * **The host file and the container file can have the same path but                                             тФВ
    >    тФВ    different content.** If `/home/Zarquan/temp/random.txt` exists on both                                        тФВ
    >    тФВ    the host and inside the `calycopis-dev` container, the application                                            тФВ
    >    тФВ    container will always see the host copy. Python tests running inside                                          тФВ
    >    тФВ    `calycopis-dev` that read the file directly (e.g. via `open()` or                                             тФВ
    >    тФВ    `hashlib`) will see the container copy, leading to mismatches.                                                тФВ
    >    тФВ  * **Containers launched via the Podman API can see each other's bind                                            тФВ
    >    тФВ    mounts.** Because both the application container and any helper                                               тФВ
    >    тФВ    containers (e.g. an Alpine container used to compute a reference                                              тФВ
    >    тФВ    checksum) are launched through the same host Podman service, they both                                        тФВ
    >    тФВ    see the host filesystem. Running `podman run -v /path:/input alpine                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ    md5sum /input` from inside `calycopis-dev` will produce the same result                                       тФВ
    >    тФВ    as the broker's application container, because both resolve `/path`                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ    against the host.                                                                                             тФВ
    >    тФВ ### Practical implications for testing                                                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ  * **Do not rely on local file I/O for reference values.** When a Python                                         тФВ
    >    тФВ    test needs to compute an expected checksum or verify file content that                                        тФВ
    >    тФВ    will be seen by an application container, it should compute the reference                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ    by running a container with the same bind mount (via `docker-py` or                                           тФВ
    >    тФВ    `podman run`), rather than reading the file directly from the                                                 тФВ
    >    тФВ    `calycopis-dev` filesystem.                                                                                   тФВ
    >    тФВ  * **Test data files must exist on the host.** If a test requires a specific                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ    file to be available as a bind mount, that file must already exist on the                                     тФВ
    >    тФВ    host filesystem at the expected path. Creating it inside the                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ    `calycopis-dev` container is not sufficient.                                                                  тФВ
    >    тФВ                                                                                                                  тФВ
